\mbox{\hyperlink{umachine_8h_af702d65cba0638c5a8194cccc8d7c39e}{U\+\_\+\+C\+F\+U\+NC}} const U\+\_\+\+I\+M\+P\+O\+RT uint8\+\_\+t {\bfseries utf8\+\_\+count\+Trail\+Bytes} \mbox{[}$\,$\mbox{]}
\end{DoxyCompactItemize}


\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
C A\+PI\+: Deprecated macros for Unicode string handling. 

The macros in \mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h}{utf\+\_\+old.\+h}} are all deprecated and their use discouraged. Some of the design principles behind the set of U\+TF macros have changed or proved impractical. Almost all of the old \char`\"{}\+U\+T\+F macros\char`\"{} are at least renamed. If you are looking for a new equivalent to an old macro, please see the comment at the old one.

Brief summary of reasons for deprecation\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item Switch on U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+S\+I\+ZE (selection of U\+T\+F-\/8/16/32 default string processing) was impractical.
\item Switch on U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+S\+A\+FE etc. (selection of unsafe/safe/strict default string processing) was of little use and impractical.
\item Whole classes of macros became obsolete outside of the U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+S\+I\+Z\+E/\+U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+S\+A\+FE selection framework\+: U\+T\+F32\+\_\+ macros (all trivial) and U\+T\+F\+\_\+ default and intermediate macros (all aliases).
\item The selection framework also caused many macro aliases.
\item Change in Unicode standard\+: \char`\"{}irregular\char`\"{} sequences (3.\+0) became illegal (3.\+2).
\item Change of language in Unicode standard\+: Growing distinction between internal x-\/bit Unicode strings and external U\+T\+F-\/x forms, with the former more lenient. Suggests renaming of U\+T\+F16\+\_\+ macros to U16\+\_\+.
\item The prefix \char`\"{}\+U\+T\+F\+\_\+\char`\"{} without a width number confused some users.
\item \char`\"{}\+Safe\char`\"{} append macros needed the addition of an error indicator output.
\item \char`\"{}\+Safe\char`\"{} U\+T\+F-\/8 macros used legitimate (if rarely used) code point values to indicate error conditions.
\item The use of the \char`\"{}\+\_\+\+C\+H\+A\+R\char`\"{} infix for code point operations confused some users.
\end{DoxyItemize}

More details\+:

Until I\+CU 2.\+2, \mbox{\hyperlink{utf_8h}{utf.\+h}} theoretically allowed to choose among U\+T\+F-\/8/16/32 for string processing, and among unsafe/safe/strict default macros for that.

It proved nearly impossible to write non-\/trivial, high-\/performance code that is U\+T\+F-\/generic. Unsafe default macros would be dangerous for default string processing, and the main reason for the \char`\"{}strict\char`\"{} versions disappeared\+: Between Unicode 3.\+0 and 3.\+2 all \char`\"{}irregular\char`\"{} U\+T\+F-\/8 sequences became illegal. The only other conditions that \char`\"{}strict\char`\"{} checked for were non-\/characters, which are valid during processing. Only during text input/output should they be checked, and at that time other well-\/formedness checks may be necessary or useful as well. This can still be done by using U16\+\_\+\+N\+E\+XT and U\+\_\+\+I\+S\+\_\+\+U\+N\+I\+C\+O\+D\+E\+\_\+\+N\+O\+N\+C\+H\+AR or U\+\_\+\+I\+S\+\_\+\+U\+N\+I\+C\+O\+D\+E\+\_\+\+C\+H\+AR.

The old U\+T\+F8\+\_\+...\+\_\+\+S\+A\+FE macros also used some normal Unicode code points to indicate malformed sequences. The new U\+T\+F8\+\_\+ macros without suffix use negative values instead.

The entire contents of \mbox{\hyperlink{utf32_8h}{utf32.\+h}} was moved here without replacement because all those macros were trivial and were meaningful only in the framework of choosing the U\+TF size.

See Jitterbug 2150 and its discussion on the I\+CU mailing list in September 2002.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


{\itshape Obsolete part} of pre-\/\+I\+CU 2.\+4 \mbox{\hyperlink{utf_8h}{utf.\+h}} file documentation\+:

The original concept for these files was for I\+CU to allow in principle to set which U\+TF (U\+T\+F-\/8/16/32) is used internally by defining U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+S\+I\+ZE to either 8, 16, or 32. \mbox{\hyperlink{utf_8h}{utf.\+h}} would then define the U\+Char type accordingly. U\+T\+F-\/16 was the default.

This concept has been abandoned. A lot of the I\+CU source code assumes U\+Char strings are in U\+T\+F-\/16. This is especially true for low-\/level code like conversion, normalization, and collation. The \mbox{\hyperlink{utf_8h}{utf.\+h}} header enforces the default of U\+T\+F-\/16. The U\+T\+F-\/8 and U\+T\+F-\/32 macros remain for now for completeness and backward compatibility.

Accordingly, \mbox{\hyperlink{utf_8h}{utf.\+h}} defines U\+Char to be an unsigned 16-\/bit integer. If this matches wchar\+\_\+t, then U\+Char is defined to be exactly wchar\+\_\+t, otherwise uint16\+\_\+t.

U\+Char32 is defined to be a signed 32-\/bit integer (int32\+\_\+t), large enough for a 21-\/bit Unicode code point (Unicode scalar value, 0..0x10ffff). Before I\+CU 2.\+4, the definition of U\+Char32 was similarly platform-\/dependent as the definition of U\+Char. For details see the documentation for U\+Char32 itself.

\mbox{\hyperlink{utf_8h}{utf.\+h}} also defines a number of C macros for handling single Unicode code points and for using U\+TF Unicode strings. It includes \mbox{\hyperlink{utf8_8h}{utf8.\+h}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{utf16_8h}{utf16.\+h}}, and \mbox{\hyperlink{utf32_8h}{utf32.\+h}} for the actual implementations of those macros and then aliases one set of them (for U\+T\+F-\/16) for general use. The U\+T\+F-\/specific macros have the U\+TF size in the macro name prefixes (U\+T\+F16\+\_\+...), while the general alias macros always begin with U\+T\+F\+\_\+...

Many string operations can be done with or without error checking. Where such a distinction is useful, there are two versions of the macros, \char`\"{}unsafe\char`\"{} and \char`\"{}safe\char`\"{} ones with ...\+\_\+\+U\+N\+S\+A\+FE and ...\+\_\+\+S\+A\+FE suffixes. The unsafe macros are fast but may cause program failures if the strings are not well-\/formed. The safe macros have an additional, boolean parameter \char`\"{}strict\char`\"{}. If strict is false, then only illegal sequences are detected. Otherwise, irregular sequences and non-\/characters are detected as well (like single surrogates). Safe macros return special error code points for illegal/irregular sequences\+: Typically, U+ffff, or values that would result in a code unit sequence of the same length as the erroneous input sequence.~\newline
 Note that \+\_\+\+U\+N\+S\+A\+FE macros have fewer parameters\+: They do not have the strictness parameter, and they do not have start/length parameters for boundary checking.

Here, the macros are aliased in two steps\+: In the first step, the U\+T\+F-\/specific macros with U\+T\+F16\+\_\+ prefix and {\itshape U\+N\+S\+A\+FE and \+\_\+\+S\+A\+FE suffixes are aliased according to the U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+S\+I\+ZE to macros with U\+TF} prefix and the same suffixes and signatures. Then, in a second step, the default, general alias macros are set to use either the unsafe or the safe/not strict (default) or the safe/strict macro; these general macros do not have a strictness parameter.

It is possible to change the default choice for the general alias macros to be unsafe, safe/not strict or safe/strict. The default is safe/not strict. It is not recommended to select the unsafe macros as the basis for Unicode string handling in I\+C\+U! To select this, define U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+S\+A\+FE, U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+S\+T\+R\+I\+CT, or U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+U\+N\+S\+A\+FE.

For general use, one should use the default, general macros with U\+T\+F\+\_\+ prefix and no {\itshape S\+A\+F\+E/\+\_\+\+U\+N\+S\+A\+FE suffix. Only in some cases it may be necessary to control the choice of macro directly and use a less generic alias. For example, if it can be assumed that a string is well-\/formed and the index will stay within the bounds, then the \+\_\+\+U\+N\+S\+A\+FE version may be used. If a U\+T\+F-\/8 string is to be processed, then the macros with U\+T\+F8} prefixes need to be used.

\DoxyHorRuler{0}


Deprecated I\+CU 2.\+4. Use the macros in \mbox{\hyperlink{utf_8h}{utf.\+h}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{utf16_8h}{utf16.\+h}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{utf8_8h}{utf8.\+h}} instead.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \#define U\+T\+F16\+\_\+\+G\+E\+T\+\_\+\+C\+H\+A\+R\+\_\+\+U\+N\+S\+A\+FE(\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{s,  }\item[{}]{i,  }\item[{}]{c }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

{\bfseries Value\+:}
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \mbox{\hyperlink{umachine_8h_abfdc26d020b4fab3ed5ca2b98fe5df43}{UPRV\_BLOCK\_MACRO\_BEGIN}} \{ \(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{    (c)=(s)[i]; \(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{    if(\mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h_ab8d1054e7a2b034ae92e824049bece53}{UTF\_IS\_SURROGATE}}(c)) \{ \(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{        if(\mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h_a01d4e0a9e33635d69fd827b5e42d5dea}{UTF\_IS\_SURROGATE\_FIRST}}(c)) \{ \(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{            (c)=\mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h_ad8b1e5a434ff14cffff805e7cc796f96}{UTF16\_GET\_PAIR\_VALUE}}((c), (s)[(i)+1]); \(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{        \} \textcolor{keywordflow}{else} \{ \(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{            (c)=\mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h_ad8b1e5a434ff14cffff805e7cc796f96}{UTF16\_GET\_PAIR\_VALUE}}((s)[(i)-\/1], (c)); \(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{        \} \(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \} \(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\} \mbox{\hyperlink{umachine_8h_a983e6cc57f8c1b0c5b9ad9ceb290418a}{UPRV\_BLOCK\_MACRO\_END}}}

\end{DoxyCode}
Get a single code point from an offset that points to any of the code units that belong to that code point. Assume 0$<$=i$<$length.

This could be used for iteration together with \mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h_a1417f8935d6f407dffc57f6c3e07edac}{U\+T\+F16\+\_\+\+C\+H\+A\+R\+\_\+\+L\+E\+N\+G\+T\+H()}} and \mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h_a77973614ec02902ab6b39a1d458dcf61}{U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+I\+S\+\_\+\+E\+R\+R\+O\+R()}}, but the use of U\+T\+F16\+\_\+\+N\+E\+X\+T\+\_\+\+C\+H\+AR\mbox{[}\+\_\+\+U\+N\+S\+A\+FE\mbox{]}() and U\+T\+F16\+\_\+\+P\+R\+E\+V\+\_\+\+C\+H\+AR\mbox{[}\+\_\+\+U\+N\+S\+A\+FE\mbox{]}() is more efficient for that. \begin{DoxyRefDesc}{Deprecated}
\item[\mbox{\hyperlink{deprecated__deprecated000143}{Deprecated}}]I\+CU 2.\+4. Renamed to U16\+\_\+\+G\+E\+T\+\_\+\+U\+N\+S\+A\+FE, see \mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h}{utf\+\_\+old.\+h}}. \end{DoxyRefDesc}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \#define U\+T\+F8\+\_\+\+B\+A\+C\+K\+\_\+\+N\+\_\+\+U\+N\+S\+A\+FE(\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{s,  }\item[{}]{i,  }\item[{}]{n }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

{\bfseries Value\+:}
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{utf__old_8h_a19b7a233154f967fad84c8113eae8b80}\label{utf__old_8h_a19b7a233154f967fad84c8113eae8b80}} 
\index{utf\_old.h@{utf\_old.h}!UTF8\_CHAR\_LENGTH@{UTF8\_CHAR\_LENGTH}}
\index{UTF8\_CHAR\_LENGTH@{UTF8\_CHAR\_LENGTH}!utf\_old.h@{utf\_old.h}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{UTF8\_CHAR\_LENGTH}{UTF8\_CHAR\_LENGTH}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \#define U\+T\+F8\+\_\+\+C\+H\+A\+R\+\_\+\+L\+E\+N\+G\+TH(\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{c }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

{\bfseries Value\+:}
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{        ((\mbox{\hyperlink{group__gtc__type__precision_ga822ca53a9ad412504532838906276a99}{uint32\_t}})(c)<=0x7f ? 1 : \(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{            ((\mbox{\hyperlink{group__gtc__type__precision_ga822ca53a9ad412504532838906276a99}{uint32\_t}})(c)<=0x7ff ? 2 : \(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{                ((\mbox{\hyperlink{group__gtc__type__precision_ga822ca53a9ad412504532838906276a99}{uint32\_t}})((c)-\/0x10000)>0xfffff ? 3 : 4) \(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{            ) \(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{        )}

\end{DoxyCode}
Given the lead character, how many bytes are taken by this code point. I\+CU does not deal with code points $>$0x10ffff unless necessary for advancing in the byte stream.

These length macros take into account that for values $>$0x10ffff the U\+T\+F8\+\_\+\+A\+P\+P\+E\+N\+D\+\_\+\+C\+H\+A\+R\+\_\+\+S\+A\+FE macros would write the error code point 0xffff with 3 bytes. Code point comparisons need to be in uint32\+\_\+t because U\+Char32 may be a signed type, and negative values must be recognized.

\begin{DoxyRefDesc}{Deprecated}
\item[\mbox{\hyperlink{deprecated__deprecated000104}{Deprecated}}]I\+CU 2.\+4. Use U8\+\_\+\+L\+E\+N\+G\+TH instead, see \mbox{\hyperlink{utf_8h}{utf.\+h}}. \end{DoxyRefDesc}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{utf__old_8h_a017b98f7de883645ec5d623ebe7c5f1c}\label{utf__old_8h_a017b98f7de883645ec5d623ebe7c5f1c}} 
\index{utf\_old.h@{utf\_old.h}!UTF8\_COUNT\_TRAIL\_BYTES@{UTF8\_COUNT\_TRAIL\_BYTES}}
\index{UTF8\_COUNT\_TRAIL\_BYTES@{UTF8\_COUNT\_TRAIL\_BYTES}!utf\_old.h@{utf\_old.h}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{UTF8\_COUNT\_TRAIL\_BYTES}{UTF8\_COUNT\_TRAIL\_BYTES}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \#define U\+T\+F8\+\_\+\+C\+O\+U\+N\+T\+\_\+\+T\+R\+A\+I\+L\+\_\+\+B\+Y\+T\+ES(\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{lead\+Byte }\end{DoxyParamCaption})~(utf8\+\_\+count\+Trail\+Bytes\mbox{[}(uint8\+\_\+t)lead\+Byte\mbox{]})}

\index{utf\_old.h@{utf\_old.h}!UTF8\_ERROR\_VALUE\_1@{UTF8\_ERROR\_VALUE\_1}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{UTF8\_ERROR\_VALUE\_1}{UTF8\_ERROR\_VALUE\_1}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \#define U\+T\+F8\+\_\+\+E\+R\+R\+O\+R\+\_\+\+V\+A\+L\+U\+E\+\_\+1~0x15}

\begin{DoxyRefDesc}{Deprecated}
\item[\mbox{\hyperlink{deprecated__deprecated000088}{Deprecated}}]I\+CU 2.\+4. Obsolete, see \mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h}{utf\+\_\+old.\+h}}. \end{DoxyRefDesc}
\begin{DoxyRefDesc}{Deprecated}
\item[\mbox{\hyperlink{deprecated__deprecated000089}{Deprecated}}]I\+CU 2.\+4. Obsolete, see \mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h}{utf\+\_\+old.\+h}}. \end{DoxyRefDesc}
U\+T\+F8\+\_\+\+E\+R\+R\+O\+R\+\_\+\+V\+A\+L\+U\+E\+\_\+1 and U\+T\+F8\+\_\+\+E\+R\+R\+O\+R\+\_\+\+V\+A\+L\+U\+E\+\_\+2 are special error values for U\+T\+F-\/8, which need 1 or 2 bytes in U\+T\+F-\/8\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{U+0015 = NAK = Negative Acknowledge, C0 control character}
\DoxyCodeLine{U+009f = highest C1 control character}
\end{DoxyCode}


These are used by U\+T\+F8\+\_\+...\+\_\+\+S\+A\+FE macros so that they can return an error value that needs the same number of code units (bytes) as were seen by a macro. They should be tested with \mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h_a77973614ec02902ab6b39a1d458dcf61}{U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+I\+S\+\_\+\+E\+R\+R\+O\+R()}} or \mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h_a40d9e02afb708312e02391210127d59b}{U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+I\+S\+\_\+\+V\+A\+L\+I\+D()}}.

\begin{DoxyRefDesc}{Deprecated}
\item[\mbox{\hyperlink{deprecated__deprecated000090}{Deprecated}}]I\+CU 2.\+4. Obsolete, see \mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h}{utf\+\_\+old.\+h}}. \end{DoxyRefDesc}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{utf__old_8h_ac21e7b820255cadabce9d1762a0a6d80}\label{utf__old_8h_ac21e7b820255cadabce9d1762a0a6d80}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{UTF\_APPEND\_CHAR}{UTF\_APPEND\_CHAR}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \#define U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+A\+P\+P\+E\+N\+D\+\_\+\+C\+H\+AR(\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{s,  }\item[{}]{i,  }\item[{}]{length,  }\item[{}]{c }\end{DoxyParamCaption})~\mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h_ae9b5d92288bc292f3c6257bf245568da}{U\+T\+F16\+\_\+\+A\+P\+P\+E\+N\+D\+\_\+\+C\+H\+A\+R\+\_\+\+S\+A\+FE}}(s, i, length, c)}

Append the code units of code point c to the string at index i and advance i to beyond the new code units (post-\/increment). The code units beginning at index i will be overwritten. Same as U\+T\+F16\+\_\+\+A\+P\+P\+E\+N\+D\+\_\+\+C\+H\+AR. \begin{DoxyPrecond}{Precondition}
0$<$=c$<$=0x10ffff 

0$<$=i$<$length 
\end{DoxyPrecond}
\begin{DoxyPostcond}{Postcondition}
0$<$i$<$=length
\end{DoxyPostcond}
\begin{DoxyRefDesc}{Deprecated}
\item[\mbox{\hyperlink{deprecated__deprecated000220}{Deprecated}}]I\+CU 2.\+4. Use U16\+\_\+\+A\+P\+P\+E\+ND instead, see \mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h}{utf\+\_\+old.\+h}}. \end{DoxyRefDesc}

\index{utf\_old.h@{utf\_old.h}!UTF\_IS\_UNICODE\_CHAR@{UTF\_IS\_UNICODE\_CHAR}}
\index{UTF\_IS\_UNICODE\_CHAR@{UTF\_IS\_UNICODE\_CHAR}!utf\_old.h@{utf\_old.h}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{UTF\_IS\_UNICODE\_CHAR}{UTF\_IS\_UNICODE\_CHAR}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \#define U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+I\+S\+\_\+\+U\+N\+I\+C\+O\+D\+E\+\_\+\+C\+H\+AR(\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{c }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

{\bfseries Value\+:}
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{    ((\mbox{\hyperlink{group__gtc__type__precision_ga822ca53a9ad412504532838906276a99}{uint32\_t}})(c)<0xd800 || \(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{        ((\mbox{\hyperlink{group__gtc__type__precision_ga822ca53a9ad412504532838906276a99}{uint32\_t}})(c)>0xdfff \&\& \(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{         (\mbox{\hyperlink{group__gtc__type__precision_ga822ca53a9ad412504532838906276a99}{uint32\_t}})(c)<=0x10ffff \&\& \(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{         !\mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h_a33f12d9f7b4299c00e4bb1805b9fb962}{UTF\_IS\_UNICODE\_NONCHAR}}(c)))}

\end{DoxyCode}
Is a given 32-\/bit value a Unicode code point value (0..U+10ffff) that can be assigned a character?

Code points that are not characters include\+:
\begin{DoxyItemize}
\item single surrogate code points (U+d800..U+dfff, 2048 code points)
\item the last two code points on each plane (U+\+\_\+\+\_\+fffe and U+\+\_\+\+\_\+ffff, 34 code points)
\item U+fdd0..U+fdef (new with Unicode 3.\+1, 32 code points)
\item the highest Unicode code point value is U+10ffff
\end{DoxyItemize}

This means that all code points below U+d800 are character code points, and that boundary is tested first for performance.

\begin{DoxyRefDesc}{Deprecated}
\item[\mbox{\hyperlink{deprecated__deprecated000097}{Deprecated}}]I\+CU 2.\+4. Renamed to U\+\_\+\+I\+S\+\_\+\+U\+N\+I\+C\+O\+D\+E\+\_\+\+C\+H\+AR, see \mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h}{utf\+\_\+old.\+h}}. \end{DoxyRefDesc}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{utf__old_8h_a33f12d9f7b4299c00e4bb1805b9fb962}\label{utf__old_8h_a33f12d9f7b4299c00e4bb1805b9fb962}} 
\index{utf\_old.h@{utf\_old.h}!UTF\_IS\_UNICODE\_NONCHAR@{UTF\_IS\_UNICODE\_NONCHAR}}
\index{UTF\_IS\_UNICODE\_NONCHAR@{UTF\_IS\_UNICODE\_NONCHAR}!utf\_old.h@{utf\_old.h}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{UTF\_IS\_UNICODE\_NONCHAR}{UTF\_IS\_UNICODE\_NONCHAR}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \#define U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+I\+S\+\_\+\+U\+N\+I\+C\+O\+D\+E\+\_\+\+N\+O\+N\+C\+H\+AR(\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{c }\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

{\bfseries Value\+:}
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{    ((c)>=0xfdd0 \&\& \(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{     ((uint32\_t)(c)<=0xfdef || ((c)\&0xfffe)==0xfffe) \&\& \(\backslash\)}
\DoxyCodeLine{     (\mbox{\hyperlink{group__gtc__type__precision_ga822ca53a9ad412504532838906276a99}{uint32\_t}})(c)<=0x10ffff)}

\end{DoxyCode}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{utf__old_8h_a32662bfc3e6226c70be758e8b594e2fe}\label{utf__old_8h_a32662bfc3e6226c70be758e8b594e2fe}}

\index{UTF\_NEXT\_CHAR@{UTF\_NEXT\_CHAR}!utf\_old.h@{utf\_old.h}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{UTF\_NEXT\_CHAR}{UTF\_NEXT\_CHAR}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \#define U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+N\+E\+X\+T\+\_\+\+C\+H\+AR(\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{s,  }\item[{}]{i,  }\item[{}]{length,  }\item[{}]{c }\end{DoxyParamCaption})~\mbox{\hyperlink{utf16_8h_a844bb48486904fdca40c8b883e9c80ee}{U16\+\_\+\+N\+E\+XT}}(s, i, length, c)}

Set c to the code point that starts at code unit i and advance i to beyond the code units of this code point (post-\/increment). i must point to the first code unit of a code point. Otherwise c is set to the trail unit (surrogate) itself. Same as U\+T\+F16\+\_\+\+N\+E\+X\+T\+\_\+\+C\+H\+AR. \begin{DoxyPrecond}{Precondition}
0$<$=i$<$length 
\end{DoxyPrecond}
\begin{DoxyPostcond}{Postcondition}
0$<$i$<$=length
\end{DoxyPostcond}
\begin{DoxyRefDesc}{Deprecated}
\item[\mbox{\hyperlink{deprecated__deprecated000219}{Deprecated}}]I\+CU 2.\+4. Renamed to U16\+\_\+\+N\+E\+XT, see \mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h}{utf\+\_\+old.\+h}}. \end{DoxyRefDesc}

\index{UTF\_PREV\_CHAR@{UTF\_PREV\_CHAR}!utf\_old.h@{utf\_old.h}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{UTF\_PREV\_CHAR}{UTF\_PREV\_CHAR}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \#define U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+P\+R\+E\+V\+\_\+\+C\+H\+AR(\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{s,  }\item[{}]{start,  }\item[{}]{i,  }\item[{}]{c }\end{DoxyParamCaption})~\mbox{\hyperlink{utf16_8h_a592fa1f80da119e1c4565dc9193c18d9}{U16\+\_\+\+P\+R\+EV}}(s, start, i, c)}

Set c to the code point that has code units before i and move i backward (towards the beginning of the string) to the first code unit of this code point (pre-\/increment). i must point to the first code unit after the last unit of a code point (i==length is allowed). Same as U\+T\+F16\+\_\+\+P\+R\+E\+V\+\_\+\+C\+H\+AR. \begin{DoxyPrecond}{Precondition}
start$<$i$<$=length 
\end{DoxyPrecond}
\begin{DoxyPostcond}{Postcondition}
start$<$=i$<$length
\end{DoxyPostcond}
\begin{DoxyRefDesc}{Deprecated}
\item[\mbox{\hyperlink{deprecated__deprecated000224}{Deprecated}}]I\+CU 2.\+4. Renamed to U16\+\_\+\+P\+R\+EV, see \mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h}{utf\+\_\+old.\+h}}. \end{DoxyRefDesc}

\mbox{\Hypertarget{utf__old_8h_a9d708c4e9dc4b4e228c17768fa826c27}\label{utf__old_8h_a9d708c4e9dc4b4e228c17768fa826c27}} 
\index{utf\_old.h@{utf\_old.h}!UTF\_SET\_CHAR\_LIMIT@{UTF\_SET\_CHAR\_LIMIT}}
\index{UTF\_SET\_CHAR\_LIMIT@{UTF\_SET\_CHAR\_LIMIT}!utf\_old.h@{utf\_old.h}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{UTF\_SET\_CHAR\_LIMIT}{UTF\_SET\_CHAR\_LIMIT}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \#define U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+S\+E\+T\+\_\+\+C\+H\+A\+R\+\_\+\+L\+I\+M\+IT(\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{s,  }\item[{}]{start,  }\item[{}]{i,  }\item[{}]{length }\end{DoxyParamCaption})~\mbox{\hyperlink{utf16_8h_a3d5ff64af4bf16cbf9a830743a5c74a4}{U16\+\_\+\+S\+E\+T\+\_\+\+C\+P\+\_\+\+L\+I\+M\+IT}}(s, start, i, length)}

Take the random-\/access index i and adjust it so that it points beyond a code point. The input index points beyond any code unit of a code point and is moved to point beyond the last code unit of the same code point. i is never decremented. In other words, if i points to a trail surrogate that is preceded by a matching lead surrogate, then i is incremented. Otherwise it is not modified. This can be used to start an iteration with \mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h_a6c009b6781036e470928d1b2e0219b2f}{U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+P\+R\+E\+V\+\_\+\+C\+H\+A\+R()}} from a random index. Same as U\+T\+F16\+\_\+\+S\+E\+T\+\_\+\+C\+H\+A\+R\+\_\+\+L\+I\+M\+IT. \begin{DoxyPrecond}{Precondition}
start$<$i$<$=length 
\end{DoxyPrecond}
\begin{DoxyPostcond}{Postcondition}
start$<$i$<$=length
\end{DoxyPostcond}
\begin{DoxyRefDesc}{Deprecated}
\item[\mbox{\hyperlink{deprecated__deprecated000227}{Deprecated}}]I\+CU 2.\+4. Renamed to U16\+\_\+\+S\+E\+T\+\_\+\+C\+P\+\_\+\+L\+I\+M\+IT, see \mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h}{utf\+\_\+old.\+h}}. \end{DoxyRefDesc}
\mbox{\Hypertarget{utf__old_8h_a323d1dd8c82f362b9e8134d3d5366ff8}\label{utf__old_8h_a323d1dd8c82f362b9e8134d3d5366ff8}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{UTF\_SET\_CHAR\_LIMIT\_UNSAFE}{UTF\_SET\_CHAR\_LIMIT\_UNSAFE}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \#define U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+S\+E\+T\+\_\+\+C\+H\+A\+R\+\_\+\+L\+I\+M\+I\+T\+\_\+\+U\+N\+S\+A\+FE(\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{s,  }\item[{}]{i }\end{DoxyParamCaption})~\mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h_ae37f17e3f06e371f107a898660be1389}{U\+T\+F16\+\_\+\+S\+E\+T\+\_\+\+C\+H\+A\+R\+\_\+\+L\+I\+M\+I\+T\+\_\+\+U\+N\+S\+A\+FE}}(s, i)}

\index{utf\_old.h@{utf\_old.h}!UTF\_SET\_CHAR\_START@{UTF\_SET\_CHAR\_START}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{UTF\_SET\_CHAR\_START}{UTF\_SET\_CHAR\_START}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \#define U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+S\+E\+T\+\_\+\+C\+H\+A\+R\+\_\+\+S\+T\+A\+RT(\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{s,  }\item[{}]{start,  }\item[{}]{i }\end{DoxyParamCaption})~\mbox{\hyperlink{utf16_8h_a31c914801f71204ee90caa6c4d0c3c1b}{U16\+\_\+\+S\+E\+T\+\_\+\+C\+P\+\_\+\+S\+T\+A\+RT}}(s, start, i)}

Take the random-\/access index i and adjust it so that it points to the beginning of a code point. The input index points to any code unit of a code point and is moved to point to the first code unit of the same code point. i is never incremented. In other words, if i points to a trail surrogate that is preceded by a matching lead surrogate, then i is decremented. Otherwise it is not modified. This can be used to start an iteration with \mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h_a32662bfc3e6226c70be758e8b594e2fe}{U\+T\+F\+\_\+\+N\+E\+X\+T\+\_\+\+C\+H\+A\+R()}} from a random index. Same as U\+T\+F16\+\_\+\+S\+E\+T\+\_\+\+C\+H\+A\+R\+\_\+\+S\+T\+A\+RT. \begin{DoxyPrecond}{Precondition}
start$<$=i$<$length 
\end{DoxyPrecond}
\begin{DoxyPostcond}{Postcondition}
start$<$=i$<$length
\end{DoxyPostcond}
\begin{DoxyRefDesc}{Deprecated}
\item[\mbox{\hyperlink{deprecated__deprecated000223}{Deprecated}}]I\+CU 2.\+4. Renamed to U16\+\_\+\+S\+E\+T\+\_\+\+C\+P\+\_\+\+S\+T\+A\+RT, see \mbox{\hyperlink{utf__old_8h}{utf\+\_\+old.\+h}}. \end{DoxyRefDesc}
